</div><div class="mw-content-ltr mw-parser-output" lang="en" dir="ltr"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Structure within the brain</div>

For the British video game developer, see <a href="/wiki/Thalamus_Ltd" title="Thalamus Ltd">Thalamus Ltd</a>. For the botanical structure, see <a href="/wiki/Receptacle_(botany)" title="Receptacle (botany)">Receptacle (botany)</a>.</div>

depiction of basic thalamus</div></td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" class="infobox-header" style="background-color: #efefef;color:inherit;">Details</th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" href="https://ifaa.unifr.ch/Public/EntryPage/TA98%20Tree/Entity%20TA98%20EN/14.1.08.601%20Entity%20TA98%20EN.htm">A14.1.08.601</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" Embryologica">TE</a></th><td class="infobox-data"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://ifaa.unifr.ch/Public/EntryPage/THE/TE2010V1.pdf#page=107?note=Linked_from_Thalamus_by_E5.14.3.4.2.1.8">E5.14.3.4.2.1.8 </a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" style="padding-right:0.25em"><a href="/wiki/Foundational_Model_of_Anatomy" title="Foundational Model of Anatomy">FMA</a></th><td class="infobox-data"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://bioportal.bioontology.org/ontologies/FMA/?p=classes&amp;conceptid=http%3A%2F%2Fpurl.org%2Fsig%2Font%2Ffma%2Ffma62007">62007</a></td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" class="infobox-below"><a href="/wiki/Anatomical_terms_of_neuroanatomy" title="Anatomical terms of neuroanatomy">Anatomical terms of neuroanatomy</a><div style="text-align: right;"><small class="noprint">&#91;<a href="https://www.wikidata.org/wiki/Q184215" class="extiw" title="d:Q184215">edit on Wikidata</a>]</small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The <b>thalamus</b> (<abbr title="plural">pl.</abbr>: <b>thalami</b>; from <a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">Greek</a> <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%CE%B8%CE%AC%CE%BB%CE%B1%CE%BC%CE%BF%CF%82" class="extiw" title="wikt:θάλαμος">θάλαμος</a>, "chamber") is a large mass of <a href="/wiki/Gray_matter" class="mw-redirect" title="Gray matter">gray matter</a> on the lateral wall of the <a href="/wiki/Third_ventricle" title="Third ventricle">third ventricle</a> forming the <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/dorsal" class="extiw" title="wikt:dorsal">dorsal</a> part of the <a href="/wiki/Diencephalon" title="Diencephalon">diencephalon</a> (a division of the <a href="/wiki/Forebrain" title="Forebrain">forebrain</a>). <a href="/wiki/Nerve_fibers" class="mw-redirect" title="Nerve fibers">Nerve fibers</a> project out of the thalamus to the <a href="/wiki/Cerebral_cortex" title="Cerebral cortex">cerebral cortex</a> in all directions, known as the <a href="/wiki/Thalamocortical_radiations" title="Thalamocortical radiations">thalamocortical radiations</a>, allowing <a href="/wiki/Hub_(network_science)" title="Hub (network science)">hub-like</a> exchanges of information. It has several functions, such as the relaying of <a href="/wiki/Sensory_neuron" title="Sensory neuron">sensory</a> and <a href="/wiki/Motor_neuron" title="Motor neuron">motor</a> signals to the cerebral cortex<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Poetics&#95;1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Poetics-1"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>1<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and the regulation of <a href="/wiki/Consciousness" title="Consciousness">consciousness</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sleep" title="Sleep">sleep</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Alertness" title="Alertness">alertness</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>3<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-Whyte2024&#95;4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Whyte2024-4"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Anatomically, the thalami are paramedian symmetrical structures (left and right), within the <a href="/wiki/Vertebrate" title="Vertebrate">vertebrate</a> brain, situated between the cerebral cortex and the <a href="/wiki/Midbrain" title="Midbrain">midbrain</a>. It forms during <a href="/wiki/Embryonic_development" class="mw-redirect" title="Embryonic development">embryonic development</a> as the main product of the diencephalon, as first recognized by the Swiss <a href="/wiki/Embryologist" class="mw-redirect" title="Embryologist">embryologist</a> and anatomist <a href="/wiki/Wilhelm_His_Sr." title="Wilhelm His Sr.">Wilhelm His Sr.</a> in 1893.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Anatomy">Anatomy</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Thalamus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Anatomy"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>The thalami are paired structures of gray matter about four centimetres long and ovoid in appearance,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> located in the <a href="/wiki/Forebrain" title="Forebrain">forebrain</a> which is superior to the <a href="/wiki/Midbrain" title="Midbrain">midbrain</a>, near the center of the brain with nerve fibers projecting out to the cerebral cortex in all directions. In fact, almost all thalamic neurons (with the notable exception of the <a href="/wiki/Thalamic_reticular_nucleus" title="Thalamic reticular nucleus">thalamic reticular nucleus</a><sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEJones1985218&#95;7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJones1985218-7"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>) project to the cerebral cortex, and every region of the cortex so far studied has been found to innervate the thalamus.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Each of the thalami may be subdivided into at least 30 <a href="/wiki/Nucleus_(neuroanatomy)" title="Nucleus (neuroanatomy)">nuclei</a>, giving a total of at least 60 for the 'whole thalamus'.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Whyte2024&#95;4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Whyte2024-4"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-Sheridan2023&#95;9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sheridan2023-9"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Estimates of the volume of the 'whole thalamus' vary. A post-mortem study of 10 people with average age 71 years found average volume 13.68 cm<span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle {}^{3}}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <msup>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

          </mrow>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mn>3</mn>
          </mrow>
        </msup>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle {}^{3}}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/2674b41dd8682789f2c17fb1d2e845d3acb793c5" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.171ex; width:1.054ex; height:2.509ex;" alt="{\displaystyle {}^{3}}"></span>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-pmid10869053&#95;10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pmid10869053-10"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In an MRI study of 12 healthy males with average age 17 years, scans showed mean 'whole thalamus' volume 8.68cm<span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle {}^{3}}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <msup>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

          </mrow>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mn>3</mn>
          </mrow>
        </msup>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle {}^{3}}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/2674b41dd8682789f2c17fb1d2e845d3acb793c5" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.171ex; width:1.054ex; height:2.509ex;" alt="{\displaystyle {}^{3}}"></span>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The medial surface of the thalamus constitutes the upper part of the lateral wall of the <a href="/wiki/Third_ventricle" title="Third ventricle">third ventricle</a>, and is connected to the corresponding surface of the opposite thalamus by a flattened gray band, the <a href="/wiki/Interthalamic_adhesion" title="Interthalamic adhesion">interthalamic adhesion</a>.
</p><p>The lateral part of the thalamus is the <a href="/wiki/Neothalamus" class="mw-redirect" title="Neothalamus">neothalamus</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Phylogenesis" title="Phylogenesis">phylogenetically</a> newest part of the thalamus, which includes the <a href="/wiki/Lateral_nuclear_group" title="Lateral nuclear group">lateral nuclei</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Pulvinar_nuclei" title="Pulvinar nuclei">pulvinar nuclei</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Medial_geniculate_nucleus" title="Medial geniculate nucleus">medial</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lateral_geniculate_nucleus" title="Lateral geniculate nucleus">lateral geniculate nuclei</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-merriam-webster&#95;12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-merriam-webster-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The surface of the thalamus is covered by two layers of <a href="/wiki/White_matter" title="White matter">white matter</a>, the <i>stratum zonale</i> covers the dorsal surface, and the <a href="/wiki/Medullary_laminae_of_thalamus" title="Medullary laminae of thalamus">external medullary lamina</a> covers the lateral surface. (This stratum zonale should not be confused with the <a href="/wiki/Superior_colliculus#Structure" title="Superior colliculus">stratum zonale</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Superior_colliculus" title="Superior colliculus">superior colliculus</a>.) The grey matter of thalamus is partitioned by a Y shaped <a href="/wiki/Internal_medullary_lamina" class="mw-redirect" title="Internal medullary lamina">internal medullary lamina</a> which divides the nuclei into anterior, medial, and lateral groups.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Tortora&#95;14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tortora-14"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>14<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-Georgescu&#95;15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Georgescu-15"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>15<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Derivatives of the <a href="/wiki/Diencephalon" title="Diencephalon">diencephalon</a> include the dorsally located <a href="/wiki/Epithalamus" title="Epithalamus">epithalamus</a> (essentially the <a href="/wiki/Habenula" title="Habenula">habenula</a> and annexes) and the peri-thalamus (pre-thalamus) containing the <a href="/wiki/Zona_incerta" title="Zona incerta">zona incerta</a> and the thalamic reticular nucleus. Due to their different <a href="/wiki/Ontogenetic" class="mw-redirect" title="Ontogenetic">ontogenetic</a> origins, the epithalamus and the peri-thalamus are formally distinguished from the thalamus proper. The <b>metathalamus</b> is made up of the lateral geniculate and medial geniculate nuclei.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-NN351hier&#95;17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NN351hier-17"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>17<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-Kiwitz&#95;2022&#95;18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kiwitz_2022-18"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>18<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The thalamus comprises a system of <a href="/wiki/Medullary_laminae_of_thalamus" title="Medullary laminae of thalamus">lamellae</a> (made up of <a href="/wiki/Myelin" title="Myelin">myelinated</a> <a href="/wiki/Axon" title="Axon">fibers</a>) that separate different thalamic subparts. Other areas are defined by distinct clusters of <a href="/wiki/Neuron" title="Neuron">neurons</a>, such as the <a href="/wiki/Periventricular_nucleus" title="Periventricular nucleus">periventricular nucleus</a>, the intralaminar elements, the "nucleus limitans", and others.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>19<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> These latter structures, different in structure from the major part of the thalamus, have been grouped together into the <i><a href="/wiki/Allothalamus" title="Allothalamus">allothalamus</a></i> as opposed to the <i><a href="/wiki/Isothalamus" title="Isothalamus">isothalamus</a></i>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>20<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> This distinction simplifies the global description of the thalamus.
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:ThalamicNuclei.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/ThalamicNuclei.svg/250px-ThalamicNuclei.svg.png" decoding="async" width="250" height="185" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/ThalamicNuclei.svg/500px-ThalamicNuclei.svg.png 1.5x" data-file-width="715" data-file-height="530" /></a><figcaption>Thalamic nuclei. <a href="/wiki/Metathalamus" class="mw-redirect" title="Metathalamus">Metathalamus</a> labelled MTh.<br />(Left thalamus viewed from left.)</figcaption></figure>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Thalmus.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Thalmus.png/250px-Thalmus.png" decoding="async" width="250" height="203" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Thalmus.png/500px-Thalmus.png 1.5x" data-file-width="1718" data-file-height="1395" /></a><figcaption>Nuclei of right thalamus<br />(viewed from above right)</figcaption></figure>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Thalamic_nuclei">Thalamic nuclei</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Thalamus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Thalamic nuclei"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_thalamic_nuclei" title="List of thalamic nuclei">List of thalamic nuclei</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Thalamus_medialgroup.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Thalamus_medialgroup.jpg/250px-Thalamus_medialgroup.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="152" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Thalamus_medialgroup.jpg/500px-Thalamus_medialgroup.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="613" data-file-height="373" /></a><figcaption>Medial nuclei of the left thalamus.<br />Key: CeM <a href="/wiki/Central_medial_nucleus" class="mw-redirect" title="Central medial nucleus">Central Medial</a>. CL <a href="/wiki/Central_lateral_nucleus" title="Central lateral nucleus">Central Lateral</a>. CM <a href="/wiki/Centromedian_nucleus" title="Centromedian nucleus">CentroMedian</a>. MD <a href="/wiki/Medial_dorsal_nucleus" title="Medial dorsal nucleus">Medial Dorsal</a>. MV MedioVentral <a href="/wiki/Reuniens_nucleus" class="mw-redirect" title="Reuniens nucleus">Reuniens</a>. Pf <a href="/wiki/Parafascicular_nucleus" class="mw-redirect" title="Parafascicular nucleus">Parafascicular</a>. (Lateral view shows sagittal section through left thalamus)</figcaption></figure>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Thalamus_lateralgroup.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Thalamus_lateralgroup.jpg/250px-Thalamus_lateralgroup.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="152" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Thalamus_lateralgroup.jpg/500px-Thalamus_lateralgroup.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="613" data-file-height="373" /></a><figcaption>Lateral nuclei of the left thalamus.<br />Key: VA <a href="/wiki/Ventral_anterior_nucleus" title="Ventral anterior nucleus">Ventral Anterior</a>. VL <a href="/wiki/Ventral_lateral_nucleus" title="Ventral lateral nucleus">Ventral Lateral</a>. VM <a href="/wiki/Ventral_medial_nucleus" class="mw-redirect" title="Ventral medial nucleus">Ventral Medial</a>. VPI Ventral PosteroInferior. VPL <a href="/wiki/Ventral_posterolateral_nucleus" title="Ventral posterolateral nucleus">Ventral PosteroLateral</a>. VPM <a href="/wiki/Ventral_posteromedial" class="mw-redirect" title="Ventral posteromedial">Ventral PosteroMedial</a>. (Medial view shows sagittal section through left thalamus.)</figcaption></figure>
<p>The principal subdivision of the thalamus into nucleus groups is the trisection of each thalamus (left and right) by a Y-shaped <a href="/wiki/Medullary_laminae_of_thalamus" title="Medullary laminae of thalamus">internal medullary lamina</a>. This trisection divides each thalamus into <a href="/wiki/Anterior_nuclei_of_thalamus" title="Anterior nuclei of thalamus">anterior</a>, <a href="/wiki/Medial_nuclear_group" class="mw-redirect" title="Medial nuclear group">medial</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lateral_nuclear_group" title="Lateral nuclear group">lateral groups</a> of nuclei.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Sheridan2023&#95;9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sheridan2023-9"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The medial group is subdivided into the <a href="/wiki/Medial_dorsal_nucleus" title="Medial dorsal nucleus">medial dorsal nucleus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Midline_nuclear_group" title="Midline nuclear group">midline group</a>. The lateral group is subdivided into <a href="/wiki/Ventral_nuclear_group" title="Ventral nuclear group">ventral</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pulvinar_nuclei" title="Pulvinar nuclei">pulvinar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lateral_dorsal_nucleus" class="mw-redirect" title="Lateral dorsal nucleus">lateral dorsal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lateral_posterior_nucleus" class="mw-redirect" title="Lateral posterior nucleus">lateral posterior</a> and metathalamus. The ventral group is further subdivided into <a href="/wiki/Ventral_anterior_nucleus" title="Ventral anterior nucleus">ventral anterior</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ventral_lateral_nucleus" title="Ventral lateral nucleus">ventral lateral</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ventral_posterior_nucleus" title="Ventral posterior nucleus">ventral posterior</a>.
</p><p>The interior medullary lamina is subdivided into <a href="/wiki/Intralaminar_thalamic_nuclei" title="Intralaminar thalamic nuclei">intralaminar nuclei</a>. Additional structures are the reticular nucleus (which envelops the lateral thalamus), the stratum zonale,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-NN374&#95;21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NN374-21"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Interthalamic_adhesion" title="Interthalamic adhesion">interthalamic adhesion</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-NN301&#95;22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NN301-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Combining these division principles yields the following hierarchy, which is subject to many further subdivisions.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Braininfo&#95;23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Braininfo-23"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>23<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>anterior group</li>
<li>medial group
<ul><li>medial dorsal nucleus</li>
<li>midline group</li></ul></li>
<li>lateral group
<ul><li>ventral group
<ul><li>ventral anterior group</li>
<li>ventral lateral group</li>
<li>ventral posterior group</li></ul></li>
<li>pulvinar group</li>
<li>lateral dorsal nucleus</li>
<li>lateral posterior nucleus</li>
<li>metathalamus
<ul><li>lateral geniculate nucleus</li>
<li>medial geniculate nucleus</li></ul></li></ul></li>
<li>intralaminar group</li>
<li>reticular nucleus</li>
<li>stratum zonale</li>
<li>interthalamic adhesion</li></ul>
<p>The term "lateral nuclear group" is used with two meanings. It can mean either the complete set of nuclei in the lateral "third" of the trisection by the lamina, or the subset which excludes the ventral group and the geniculate nuclei.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>24<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>25<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Blood_supply">Blood supply</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Thalamus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Blood supply"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>The thalamus derives its blood supply from a number of arteries: the polar artery (<a href="/wiki/Posterior_communicating_artery" title="Posterior communicating artery">posterior communicating artery</a>), paramedian thalamic-subthalamic arteries, inferolateral (thalamogeniculate) arteries, and <a href="/wiki/Posterior_cerebral_artery#(Posterior)_choroidal_branches" title="Posterior cerebral artery">posterior (medial and lateral) choroidal arteries</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Torrico2023&#95;26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Torrico2023-26"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>26<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>27<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> These are all branches of the <a href="/wiki/Posterior_cerebral_artery" title="Posterior cerebral artery">posterior cerebral artery</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Sheridan2023&#95;9-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sheridan2023-9"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>28<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Some people have the <a href="/wiki/Artery_of_Percheron" title="Artery of Percheron">artery of Percheron</a>, which is a rare anatomic variation in which a single arterial trunk arises from the posterior cerebral artery to supply both parts of the thalamus.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Connections">Connections</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Thalamus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Connections"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Spinal_cord_tracts_-_English.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Spinal_cord_tracts_-_English.svg/250px-Spinal_cord_tracts_-_English.svg.png" decoding="async" width="250" height="108" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Spinal_cord_tracts_-_English.svg/500px-Spinal_cord_tracts_-_English.svg.png 1.5x" data-file-width="874" data-file-height="376" /></a><figcaption>The thalamus is connected to the spinal cord via the <a href="/wiki/Spinothalamic_tract" title="Spinothalamic tract">spinothalamic tract</a></figcaption></figure>
<p>The thalamus has many connections to the hippocampus via the <a href="/wiki/Mammillothalamic_tract" title="Mammillothalamic tract">mammillothalamic tract</a>. This tract comprises the <a href="/wiki/Mammillary_bodies" class="mw-redirect" title="Mammillary bodies">mammillary bodies</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fornix_(neuroanatomy)" title="Fornix (neuroanatomy)">fornix</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-pmid21255590&#95;29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pmid21255590-29"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>29<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The thalamus is connected to the <a href="/wiki/Cerebral_cortex" title="Cerebral cortex">cerebral cortex</a> via the <a href="/wiki/Thalamocortical_radiations" title="Thalamocortical radiations">thalamocortical radiations</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>30<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Spinothalamic_tract" title="Spinothalamic tract">spinothalamic tract</a> is a sensory pathway originating in the spinal cord. It transmits information to the thalamus about pain, temperature, itch and <a href="/wiki/Crude_touch" class="mw-redirect" title="Crude touch">crude touch</a>. There are two main parts: the <a href="/wiki/Lateral_spinothalamic_tract" class="mw-redirect" title="Lateral spinothalamic tract">lateral spinothalamic tract</a>, which transmits pain and temperature, and the <a href="/wiki/Anterior_spinothalamic_tract" class="mw-redirect" title="Anterior spinothalamic tract">anterior (or ventral) spinothalamic tract</a>, which transmits crude touch and pressure.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Function">Function</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Thalamus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Function"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>The thalamus has multiple functions, and is generally believed to act as a relay station, or <a href="/wiki/Hub_(network_science)" title="Hub (network science)">hub</a>, relaying information between different subcortical areas and the cerebral cortex.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>31<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In particular, every sensory system (with the exception of the <a href="/wiki/Olfactory_system" title="Olfactory system">olfactory system</a>) includes a thalamic nucleus that receives sensory signals and sends them to the associated primary cortical area.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>32<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>33<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>For the visual system, for example, inputs from the <a href="/wiki/Retina" title="Retina">retina</a> are sent to the <a href="/wiki/Lateral_geniculate_nucleus" title="Lateral geniculate nucleus">lateral geniculate nucleus</a> of the thalamus, which in turn projects to the <a href="/wiki/Visual_cortex" title="Visual cortex">visual cortex</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Occipital_lobe" title="Occipital lobe">occipital lobe</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>34<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Similarly the <a href="/wiki/Medial_geniculate_nucleus" title="Medial geniculate nucleus">medial geniculate nucleus</a> acts as a key <a href="/wiki/Auditory_system" title="Auditory system">auditory</a> relay between the <a href="/wiki/Inferior_colliculus" title="Inferior colliculus">inferior colliculus</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Midbrain" title="Midbrain">midbrain</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Primary_auditory_cortex" class="mw-redirect" title="Primary auditory cortex">primary auditory cortex</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> The <a href="/wiki/Ventral_posterior_nucleus" title="Ventral posterior nucleus">ventral posterior nucleus</a> is a key <a href="/wiki/Somatosensory" class="mw-redirect" title="Somatosensory">somatosensory</a> relay, which sends touch and <a href="/wiki/Proprioceptive" class="mw-redirect" title="Proprioceptive">proprioceptive</a> information to the <a href="/wiki/Primary_somatosensory_cortex" title="Primary somatosensory cortex">primary somatosensory cortex</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> In rodents, proprioceptive information of head and whisker movements is integrated already at the thalamic level.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>35<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The thalamus is believed to both process sensory information as well as relay it—each of the primary sensory relay areas receives strong feedback connections from the cerebral cortex.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>36<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The thalamus also plays an important role in regulating states of <a href="/wiki/Sleep" title="Sleep">sleep</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Wakefulness" title="Wakefulness">wakefulness</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>37<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Thalamic nuclei have strong reciprocal connections with the cerebral cortex, forming <a href="/wiki/Thalamo-cortico-thalamic_circuits" title="Thalamo-cortico-thalamic circuits">thalamo-cortico-thalamic circuits</a> that are believed to be involved with <a href="/wiki/Consciousness" title="Consciousness">consciousness</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>38<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>39<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The thalamus plays a major role in regulating arousal, the level of awareness, and activity. Damage to the thalamus can lead to permanent <a href="/wiki/Coma" title="Coma">coma</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>40<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The role of the thalamus in the more anterior <a href="/wiki/Pallidal" class="mw-redirect" title="Pallidal">pallidal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nigral" class="mw-redirect" title="Nigral">nigral</a> territories in the <a href="/wiki/Basal_ganglia" title="Basal ganglia">basal ganglia</a> system disturbances is recognized but still poorly understood. The contribution of the thalamus to vestibular or to <a href="/wiki/Tectal" class="mw-redirect" title="Tectal">tectal</a> functions is almost ignored. The thalamus has been thought of as a "relay" that simply forwards signals to the cerebral cortex. Newer research suggests that thalamic function is more selective.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>41<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Many different functions are linked to various regions of the thalamus. This is the case for many of the sensory systems (except for the olfactory system), such as the <a href="/wiki/Auditory_system" title="Auditory system">auditory</a>, <a href="/wiki/Somatic_sensory_system" class="mw-redirect" title="Somatic sensory system">somatic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Visceral" class="mw-redirect" title="Visceral">visceral</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gustatory" class="mw-redirect" title="Gustatory">gustatory</a> and <a href="/wiki/Visual_system" title="Visual system">visual systems</a> where localized lesions provoke specific sensory deficits. A major role of the thalamus is support of motor and language systems, and much of the circuitry implicated for these systems is shared.
</p><p>The thalamus is <i>functionally connected</i> to the <a href="/wiki/Hippocampus" title="Hippocampus">hippocampus</a><sup id="cite&#95;ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>42<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> as part of the extended hippocampal system at the thalamic anterior nuclei.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>43<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> With respect to spatial memory and spatial sensory datum they are crucial for human episodic event memory.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>44<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>45<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The thalamic region's connection to the <a href="/wiki/Medial_temporal_lobe" class="mw-redirect" title="Medial temporal lobe">medial temporal lobe</a> provides differentiation of the functioning of recollective and familiarity memory.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-pmid21255590&#95;29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pmid21255590-29"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>29<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The neuronal information processes necessary for motor control were proposed as a network involving the thalamus as a subcortical motor center.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>46<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Through investigations of the anatomy of the brains of primates<sup id="cite&#95;ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>47<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> the nature of the interconnected tissues of the <a href="/wiki/Cerebellum" title="Cerebellum">cerebellum</a> to the multiple motor cortices suggested that the thalamus fulfills a key function in providing the specific channels from the basal ganglia and cerebellum to the cortical motor areas.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>48<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>49<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In an investigation of the <a href="/wiki/Saccade" title="Saccade">saccade</a> and <a href="/wiki/Antisaccade_task" title="Antisaccade task">antisaccade</a><sup id="cite&#95;ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>50<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> motor response in three monkeys, the thalamic regions were found to be involved in the generation of antisaccade eye-movement (that is, the ability to inhibit the reflexive ballistic movement of the eyes in the direction of a presented stimulus).<sup id="cite&#95;ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>51<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Recent research suggests that the mediodorsal thalamus (MD) may play a broader role in cognition. Specifically, the mediodorsal thalamus may "amplify the connectivity (signaling strength) of just the circuits in the cortex appropriate for the current context and thereby contribute to the flexibility (of the mammalian brain) to make complex decisions by wiring the many associations on which decisions depend into weakly connected cortical circuits."<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:0&#95;52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-52"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>52<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Researchers found that "enhancing MD activity magnified the ability of mice to "think,"<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:0&#95;52-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-52"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>52<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> driving down by more than 25 percent their error rate in deciding which conflicting sensory stimuli to follow to find the reward."<sup id="cite&#95;ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>53<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Development">Development</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Thalamus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Development"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>The thalamic complex is composed of the perithalamus (or prethalamus, previously also known as ventral thalamus), the mid-diencephalic organiser (which forms later the <a href="/wiki/Zona_limitans_intrathalamica" title="Zona limitans intrathalamica">zona limitans intrathalamica</a> (ZLI) ) and the thalamus (dorsal thalamus).<sup id="cite&#95;ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>54<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>55<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The development of the thalamus can be subdivided into three steps.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-cell&#95;56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cell-56"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>56<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
The thalamus is the largest structure deriving from the embryonic <a href="/wiki/Diencephalon" title="Diencephalon">diencephalon</a>, the posterior part of the forebrain situated between the midbrain and the cerebrum.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Early_brain_development">Early brain development</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Thalamus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Early brain development"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>After <a href="/wiki/Neurulation" title="Neurulation">neurulation</a>, the early developmental stage (<a href="/wiki/Primordium" title="Primordium">primordium</a>) of the <a href="/wiki/Prethalamus" class="mw-redirect" title="Prethalamus">prethalamus</a> and the thalamus is induced within the <a href="/wiki/Neural_tube" title="Neural tube">neural tube</a>. Data from different vertebrate model organisms support a model in which the interaction between two <a href="/wiki/Transcription_factor" title="Transcription factor">transcription factors</a>, Fez and Otx, is of decisive importance. Fez is expressed in the prethalamus, and functional experiments show that Fez is required for prethalamus formation.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>57<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>58<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Posteriorly, <a href="/wiki/OTX1" title="OTX1">OTX1</a> and <a href="/wiki/OTX2" class="mw-redirect" title="OTX2">OTX2</a> abut the expression domain of Fez and are required for proper development of the thalamus.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>59<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>60<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Formation_of_progenitor_domains">Formation of progenitor domains</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Thalamus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Formation of progenitor domains"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Early in thalamic development two progenitor domains form, a caudal domain, and a rostral domain. The caudal domain gives rise to all of the glutamatergic neurons in the adult thalamus while the rostral domain gives rise to all of the GABAergic neurons in the adult thalamus.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>61<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="The_formation_of_the_mid-diencephalic_organiser_(MDO)"><span id="The_formation_of_the_mid-diencephalic_organiser_.28MDO.29"></span>The formation of the mid-diencephalic organiser (MDO)</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Thalamus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: The formation of the mid-diencephalic organiser (MDO)"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>At the interface between the expression domains of Fez and Otx, the mid-diencephalic organizer (MDO, also called the ZLI organiser) is induced within the thalamic <a href="/wiki/Primordium" title="Primordium">anlage</a>. The MDO is the central signalling organizer in the thalamus. A lack of the organizer leads to the absence of the thalamus. The MDO matures from ventral to dorsal during development. Members of the <a href="/wiki/Sonic_hedgehog" class="mw-redirect" title="Sonic hedgehog">sonic hedgehog</a> (SHH) family and of the <a href="/wiki/Wnt_signaling_pathway" title="Wnt signaling pathway">Wnt</a> family are the main principal signals emitted by the MDO.
</p><p>Besides its importance as signalling center, the organizer matures into the morphological structure of the <a href="/wiki/Zona_limitans_intrathalamica" title="Zona limitans intrathalamica">zona limitans intrathalamica</a> (ZLI).
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Maturation_and_parcellation_of_the_thalamus">Maturation and parcellation of the thalamus</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Thalamus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Maturation and parcellation of the thalamus"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>After its induction, the MDO starts to orchestrate the development of the thalamic anlage by release of signalling molecules such as SHH.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>62<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In mice, the function of signaling at the MDO has not been addressed directly due to a complete absence of the <a href="/wiki/Diencephalon" title="Diencephalon">diencephalon</a> in SHH mutants.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>63<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Studies in chicks have shown that SHH is both necessary and sufficient for thalamic gene induction.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>64<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Zebrafish" title="Zebrafish">zebrafish</a>, it was shown that the expression of two SHH genes, SHH-a and SHH-b (formerly described as twhh) mark the MDO territory, and that SHH signaling is sufficient for the molecular differentiation of both the prethalamus and the thalamus but is not required for their maintenance and SHH signaling from the MDO/alar plate is sufficient for the maturation of prethalamic and thalamic territory while ventral Shh signals are dispensable.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>65<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The exposure to SHH leads to differentiation of thalamic neurons. SHH signaling from the MDO induces a posterior-to-anterior wave of expression the proneural gene <a href="/wiki/Neurogenins" title="Neurogenins">Neurogenin1</a> in the major (caudal) part of the thalamus, and Ascl1 (formerly Mash1) in the remaining narrow stripe of rostral thalamic cells immediately adjacent to the MDO, and in the prethalamus.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>66<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>67<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>This zonation of proneural gene expression leads to the differentiation of glutamatergic relay neurons from the Neurogenin1+ precursors and of GABAergic inhibitory neurons from the Ascl1+ precursors. In fish, selection of these alternative neurotransmitter fates is controlled by the dynamic expression of Her6 the homolog of <a href="/wiki/HES1" title="HES1">HES1</a>. Expression of this hairy-like bHLH <a href="/wiki/Transcription_factor" title="Transcription factor">transcription factor</a>, which represses Neurogenin but is required for Ascl1, is progressively lost from the caudal thalamus but maintained in the prethalamus and in the stripe of rostral thalamic cells. In addition, studies on chick and mice have shown that blocking the Shh pathway leads to absence of the rostral thalamus and substantial decrease of the caudal thalamus. The rostral thalamus will give rise to the reticular nucleus mainly whereby the caudal thalamus will form the relay thalamus and will be further subdivided in the <a href="/wiki/Thalamic_nuclei" class="mw-redirect" title="Thalamic nuclei">thalamic nuclei</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-cell&#95;56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cell-56"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>56<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In humans, a common genetic variation in the promoter region of the <a href="/wiki/Serotonin_transporter" title="Serotonin transporter">serotonin transporter</a> (the SERT-long and -short allele: <a href="/wiki/5-HTTLPR" title="5-HTTLPR">5-HTTLPR</a>) has been shown to affect the development of several regions of the thalamus in adults. People who inherit two short <a href="/wiki/Allele" title="Allele">alleles</a> (SERT-ss) have more neurons and a larger volume in the <a href="/wiki/Pulvinar_nucleus" class="mw-redirect" title="Pulvinar nucleus">pulvinar</a> and possibly the limbic regions of the thalamus. Enlargement of the thalamus provides an anatomical basis for why people who inherit two SERT-ss alleles are more vulnerable to <a href="/wiki/Major_depressive_disorder" title="Major depressive disorder">major depression</a>, <a href="/wiki/Post-traumatic_stress_disorder" title="Post-traumatic stress disorder">post-traumatic stress disorder</a>, and suicide.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>68<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Clinical_significance">Clinical significance</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Thalamus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Clinical significance"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>A thalamus damaged by a <a href="/wiki/Stroke" title="Stroke">stroke</a> can lead to <a href="/wiki/Thalamic_pain_syndrome" class="mw-redirect" title="Thalamic pain syndrome">thalamic pain syndrome</a>,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>69<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> which involves a one-sided burning or aching sensation often accompanied by <a href="/wiki/Mood_disorder" title="Mood disorder">mood swings</a>. Bilateral <a href="/wiki/Ischemia" title="Ischemia">ischemia</a> of the area supplied by the paramedian artery can cause serious problems including <a href="/wiki/Akinetic_mutism" title="Akinetic mutism">akinetic mutism</a>, and be accompanied by <a href="/wiki/Oculomotor" class="mw-redirect" title="Oculomotor">oculomotor</a> problems. A related concept is <a href="/wiki/Thalamocortical_dysrhythmia" title="Thalamocortical dysrhythmia">thalamocortical dysrhythmia</a>. The occlusion of the <a href="/wiki/Artery_of_Percheron" title="Artery of Percheron">artery of Percheron</a> can lead to a bilateral thalamus infarction.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Korsakoff_syndrome" title="Korsakoff syndrome">Korsakoff syndrome</a> stems from damage to the <a href="/wiki/Mammillary_body" title="Mammillary body">mammillary body</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Mammillothalamic_fasciculus" class="mw-redirect" title="Mammillothalamic fasciculus">mammillothalamic fasciculus</a> or the thalamus.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Kopelman&#95;70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kopelman-70"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>70<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-AJNR&#95;71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AJNR-71"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>71<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Fatal_familial_insomnia" class="mw-redirect" title="Fatal familial insomnia">Fatal familial insomnia</a> is a hereditary <a href="/wiki/Prion" title="Prion">prion</a> disease in which degeneration of the thalamus occurs, causing the patient to gradually lose their ability to sleep and progressing to a state of total <a href="/wiki/Insomnia" title="Insomnia">insomnia</a>, which invariably leads to death. In contrast, damage to the thalamus can result in coma.
</p><p>Atrophy of the thalamus is an indicator of the start of <a href="/wiki/Multiple_sclerosis" title="Multiple sclerosis">multiple sclerosis</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>72<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>73<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="Updated version https&#58;//www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/37770560 (July 2025)">needs update</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Thalamic volume loss by atrophy, is also significantly shown in sporadic <a href="/wiki/Frontotemporal_dementia" title="Frontotemporal dementia">frontotemporal dementia</a>, noted in the anterior-dorsal thickness.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Khadhraoui&#95;74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Khadhraoui-74"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>74<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Microstimulation of the posterior portion of the <a href="/wiki/Ventral_lateral_nucleus#Subdivisions" title="Ventral lateral nucleus">ventral medial thalamic nucleus</a> can be used to evoke pain, temperature and visceral sensations.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>75<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Krista_and_Tatiana_Hogan" title="Krista and Tatiana Hogan">Krista and Tatiana Hogan</a> have a unique thalamic connection that may provide insight into the philosophical and neurological foundations of consciousness. It has been argued that there's no empirical test that can conclusively establish that for some sensations, the twins share one token experience rather than two exactly matching token experiences. Yet background considerations about the way the brain has specific locations for conscious contents, combined with the evident overlapping pathways in the twins' brains, arguably implies that the twins share some conscious experiences. If this is true, then the twins may offer a proof of concept for how experiences in general could be shared between brains.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Cochrane&#95;76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cochrane-76"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>76<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>77<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>78<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>

<ul><li>→ <i><a href="/wiki/Sensory_decussation" title="Sensory decussation">sensory decussation</a>/arcuate fibers</i> (<a href="/wiki/Posterior_external_arcuate_fibers" class="mw-redirect" title="Posterior external arcuate fibers">Posterior external arcuate fibers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Internal_arcuate_fibers" title="Internal arcuate fibers">Internal arcuate fibers</a>) → <a href="/wiki/Medial_lemniscus" title="Medial lemniscus">Medial lemniscus</a>/<a href="/wiki/Trigeminal_lemniscus" title="Trigeminal lemniscus">Trigeminal lemniscus</a> → <a class="mw-selflink selflink">Thalamus</a> (<a href="/wiki/Ventral_posterolateral_nucleus" title="Ventral posterolateral nucleus">VPL</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ventral_posteromedial_nucleus" title="Ventral posteromedial nucleus">VPM</a>)</li></ul>

<ul><li>→ <a href="/wiki/Posterior_limb_of_internal_capsule" class="mw-redirect" title="Posterior limb of internal capsule">Posterior limb of internal capsule</a> → <a href="/wiki/Postcentral_gyrus" title="Postcentral gyrus">Postcentral gyrus</a></li></ul>
</div></td></tr></tbody></table><div></div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="navbox-group" style="width:1%"><a href="/wiki/Anterolateral_system" class="mw-redirect" title="Anterolateral system">Anterolateral</a>/<br /><a href="/wiki/Pain" title="Pain">pain</a></th><td class="navbox-list-with-group navbox-list navbox-odd" style="width:100%;padding:0"><div style="padding:0 0.25em"></div><table class="nowraplinks navbox-subgroup" style="border-spacing:0"><tbody><tr><th scope="row" class="navbox-group" style="width:1%"><a href="/wiki/Nociception#Neospinothalamic_tract" title="Nociception">Fast</a>/lateral</th><td class="navbox-list-with-group navbox-list navbox-even" style="width:100%;padding:0"><div style="padding:0 0.25em">
<ul><li>1° (<a href="/wiki/Free_nerve_ending" title="Free nerve ending">Free nerve ending</a> → <a href="/wiki/A_delta_fiber" class="mw-redirect" title="A delta fiber">A delta fiber</a>) → 2° (<a href="/wiki/Anterior_white_commissure" title="Anterior white commissure">Anterior white commissure</a> → <b><a href="/wiki/Lateral_spinothalamic_tract" class="mw-redirect" title="Lateral spinothalamic tract">Lateral</a> and <a href="/wiki/Anterior_spinothalamic_tract" class="mw-redirect" title="Anterior spinothalamic tract">Anterior</a> <a href="/wiki/Spinothalamic_tract" title="Spinothalamic tract">Spinothalamic tract</a></b> → <a href="/wiki/Spinothalamic_tract" title="Spinothalamic tract">Spinal lemniscus</a> → <a href="/wiki/Ventral_posterolateral_nucleus" title="Ventral posterolateral nucleus">VPL</a> of <a class="mw-selflink selflink">Thalamus</a>) → 3° (<a href="/wiki/Postcentral_gyrus" title="Postcentral gyrus">Postcentral gyrus</a>) → 4° (<a href="/wiki/Posterior_parietal_cortex" title="Posterior parietal cortex">Posterior parietal cortex</a>)</li></ul>
<p>2° (<b><a href="/wiki/Spinomesencephalic_tract" class="mw-redirect" title="Spinomesencephalic tract">Spinomesencephalic tract</a></b> → <a href="/wiki/Superior_colliculus" title="Superior colliculus">Superior colliculus</a> of <a href="/wiki/Midbrain_tectum" class="mw-redirect" title="Midbrain tectum">Midbrain tectum</a>)
</p>
</div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="navbox-group" style="width:1%"><a href="/wiki/Nociception#Paleospinothalamic_tract" title="Nociception">Slow</a>/medial</th><td class="navbox-list-with-group navbox-list navbox-odd" style="width:100%;padding:0"><div style="padding:0 0.25em">
<ul><li>1° (<a href="/wiki/Group_C_nerve_fiber" title="Group C nerve fiber">Group C nerve fiber</a> → <b><a href="/wiki/Spinoreticular_tract" title="Spinoreticular tract">Spinoreticular tract</a></b> → <a href="/wiki/Reticular_formation" title="Reticular formation">Reticular formation</a>) → 2° (<a href="/wiki/Medial_dorsal_nucleus" title="Medial dorsal nucleus">MD</a> of <a class="mw-selflink selflink">Thalamus</a>) → 3° (<a href="/wiki/Cingulate_cortex" title="Cingulate cortex">Cingulate cortex</a>)</li></ul>
</div></td></tr></tbody></table><div></div></td></tr></tbody></table><div></div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="navbox-group" style="width:1%">Motor</th><td class="navbox-list-with-group navbox-list navbox-odd hlist" style="width:100%;padding:0"><div style="padding:0 0.25em"></div><table class="nowraplinks navbox-subgroup" style="border-spacing:0"><tbody><tr><th scope="row" class="navbox-group" style="width:1%"><a href="/wiki/Pyramidal_tracts" title="Pyramidal tracts">Pyramidal</a></th><td class="navbox-list-with-group navbox-list navbox-even" style="width:100%;padding:0"><div style="padding:0 0.25em">
<ul><li><i>flexion:</i> <a href="/wiki/Primary_motor_cortex" title="Primary motor cortex">Primary motor cortex</a> → <a href="/wiki/Posterior_limb_of_internal_capsule" class="mw-redirect" title="Posterior limb of internal capsule">Posterior limb of internal capsule</a> → <a href="/wiki/Decussation_of_pyramids" class="mw-redirect" title="Decussation of pyramids">Decussation of pyramids</a> → <b><a href="/wiki/Pyramidal_tracts" title="Pyramidal tracts">Corticospinal tract</a> (<a href="/wiki/Lateral_corticospinal_tract" title="Lateral corticospinal tract">Lateral</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anterior_corticospinal_tract" title="Anterior corticospinal tract">Anterior</a>)</b> → <a href="/wiki/Neuromuscular_junction" title="Neuromuscular junction">Neuromuscular junction</a></li></ul>
</div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="navbox-group" style="width:1%"><a href="/wiki/Extrapyramidal_system" title="Extrapyramidal system">Extrapyramidal</a></th><td class="navbox-list-with-group navbox-list navbox-odd" style="width:100%;padding:0"><div style="padding:0 0.25em"></div><table class="nowraplinks navbox-subgroup" style="border-spacing:0"><tbody><tr><th scope="row" class="navbox-group" style="width:1%"><span class="nobold"><i>flexion:</i></span></th><td class="navbox-list-with-group navbox-list navbox-odd" style="width:100%;padding:0"><div style="padding:0 0.25em">
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Primary_motor_cortex" title="Primary motor cortex">Primary motor cortex</a> → <a href="/wiki/Genu_of_internal_capsule" class="mw-redirect" title="Genu of internal capsule">Genu of internal capsule</a> → <b><a href="/wiki/Corticobulbar_tract" title="Corticobulbar tract">Corticobulbar tract</a></b>  → <a href="/wiki/Facial_motor_nucleus" title="Facial motor nucleus">Facial motor nucleus</a> → <a href="/wiki/Facial_muscles" title="Facial muscles">Facial muscles</a></li></ul>
</div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="navbox-group" style="width:1%"><span class="nobold"><i>flexion:</i></span></th><td class="navbox-list-with-group navbox-list navbox-even" style="width:100%;padding:0"><div style="padding:0 0.25em">
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Red_nucleus" title="Red nucleus">Red nucleus</a> → <b><a href="/wiki/Rubrospinal_tract" title="Rubrospinal tract">Rubrospinal tract</a></b></li></ul>
</div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="navbox-group" style="width:1%"><span class="nobold"><i>extension:</i></span></th><td class="navbox-list-with-group navbox-list navbox-odd" style="width:100%;padding:0"><div style="padding:0 0.25em">
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Anatomy_of_the_cerebellum#Phylogenetic_and_functional_divisions" title="Anatomy of the cerebellum"> Vestibulocerebellum</a> →  <a href="/wiki/Vestibular_nuclei" title="Vestibular nuclei">Vestibular nuclei</a> → <b><a href="/wiki/Vestibulospinal_tract" title="Vestibulospinal tract">Vestibulospinal tract</a></b></li></ul>
</div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="navbox-group" style="width:1%"><span class="nobold"><i>extension:</i></span></th><td class="navbox-list-with-group navbox-list navbox-even" style="width:100%;padding:0"><div style="padding:0 0.25em">
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Anatomy_of_the_cerebellum#Phylogenetic_and_functional_divisions" title="Anatomy of the cerebellum"> Vestibulocerebellum</a> → <a href="/wiki/Reticular_formation" title="Reticular formation">Reticular formation</a> → <b><a href="/wiki/Reticular_formation#Descending_reticulospinal_tracts" title="Reticular formation">Reticulospinal tract</a></b></li></ul>
</div></td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" class="navbox-list navbox-odd" style="width:100%;padding:0"><div style="padding:0 0.25em">
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Midbrain_tectum" class="mw-redirect" title="Midbrain tectum">Midbrain tectum</a> → <b><a href="/wiki/Tectospinal_tract" title="Tectospinal tract">Tectospinal tract</a></b>  → muscles of neck</li></ul>
</div></td></tr></tbody></table><div></div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="navbox-group" style="width:1%"><a href="/wiki/Basal_ganglia" title="Basal ganglia">Basal ganglia</a></th><td style="border-spacing:0"><tbody><tr><th scope="row" class="navbox-group" style="width:1%"><span class="nobold"><a href="/wiki/Direct_pathway_of_movement" class="mw-redirect" title="Direct pathway of movement"><i>direct:</i></a></span></th><td class="navbox-list-with-group navbox-list navbox-even" style="width:100%;padding:0"><div style="padding:0 0.25em">1° (<a href="/wiki/Motor_cortex" title="Motor cortex">Motor cortex</a> → <a href="/wiki/Striatum" title="Striatum">Striatum</a>) → 2° (<a href="/wiki/Medial_globus_pallidus" class="mw-redirect" title="Medial globus pallidus">GPi</a>) → 3° (<a href="/wiki/Lenticular_fasciculus" title="Lenticular fasciculus">Lenticular fasciculus</a>/<a href="/wiki/Ansa_lenticularis" title="Ansa lenticularis">Ansa lenticularis</a> → <a href="/wiki/Thalamic_fasciculus" title="Thalamic fasciculus">Thalamic fasciculus</a> → <a href="/wiki/Ventral_lateral_nucleus" title="Ventral lateral nucleus">VL</a> of <a class="mw-selflink selflink">Thalamus</a>) → 4° (<a href="/wiki/Thalamocortical_radiations" title="Thalamocortical radiations">Thalamocortical radiations</a> → <a href="/wiki/Supplementary_motor_area" class="navbox-list-with-group navbox-list navbox-odd" style="width:100%;padding:0"><div style="padding:0 0.25em">1° (<a href="/wiki/Motor_cortex" title="Motor cortex">Motor cortex</a> → <a href="/wiki/Striatum" title="Striatum">Striatum</a>) → 2° (<a href="/wiki/Lateral_globus_pallidus" class="mw-redirect" title="Lateral globus pallidus">GPe</a>) → 3° (<a href="/wiki/Subthalamic_fasciculus" title="Subthalamic fasciculus">Subthalamic fasciculus</a> → <a href="/wiki/Subthalamic_nucleus" title="Subthalamic nucleus">Subthalamic nucleus</a>) → 4° (<a href="/wiki/Subthalamic_fasciculus" title="Subthalamic fasciculus">Subthalamic fasciculus</a> → <a href="/wiki/Medial_globus_pallidus" class="mw-redirect" title="Medial globus pallidus">GPi</a>) → 5° (<a href="/wiki/Lenticular_fasciculus" title="Lenticular fasciculus">Lenticular fasciculus</a>/<a href="/wiki/Ansa_lenticularis" title="Ansa lenticularis">Ansa lenticularis</a> → <a href="/wiki/Thalamic_fasciculus" title="Thalamic fasciculus">Thalamic fasciculus</a> → <a href="/wiki/Ventral_lateral_nucleus" title="Ventral lateral nucleus">VL</a> of <a class="mw-selflink selflink">Thalamus</a>) → 6° (<a href="/wiki/Thalamocortical_radiations" title="Thalamocortical radiations">Thalamocortical radiations</a> → <a href="/wiki/Supplementary_motor_area" title="Supplementary motor area">Supplementary motor area</a>) →  7° (<a href="/wiki/Motor_cortex" title="Motor cortex">Motor cortex</a>)</div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="navbox-group" navbox-even" style="width:100%;padding:0"><div style="padding:0 0.25em">
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Substantia_nigra_pars_compacta" class="mw-redirect" title="Substantia nigra pars compacta">Pars compacta</a> → <a href="/wiki/Striatum" title="Striatum">Striatum</a></li></ul>
</div></td></tr></tbody></table><div></div></td></tr></tbody></table><div></div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="navbox-group" style="width:1%"><a href="/wiki/Cerebellum" title="Cerebellum">Cerebellar</a></th><td class="navbox-list-with-group navbox-list navbox-odd hlist" style="width:100%;padding:0"><div style="padding:0 0.25em"></div><table class="nowraplinks navbox-subgroup" style="border-spacing:0"><tbody><tr><th scope="row" class="navbox-group" style="width:1%">Afferent</th><td class="navbox-list-with-group navbox-list navbox-odd" style="width:100%;padding:0"><div style="padding:0 0.25em">
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Vestibular_nuclei" title="Vestibular nuclei">Vestibular nuclei</a> → <b><a href="/wiki/Vestibulocerebellar_tract" title="Vestibulocerebellar tract">Vestibulocerebellar tract</a></b> → <a href="/wiki/Inferior_cerebellar_peduncle" title="Inferior cerebellar peduncle">ICP</a> → <a href="/wiki/Cerebellum" title="Cerebellum">Cerebellum</a> → <a href="/wiki/Cerebellum_granule_cell" class="mw-redirect" title="Cerebellum granule cell">Granule cell</a></li></ul>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Pontine_nuclei" title="Pontine nuclei">Pontine nuclei</a> → <b><a href="/wiki/Pontocerebellar_fibers" title="Pontocerebellar fibers">Pontocerebellar fibers</a></b> → <a href="/wiki/Middle_cerebellar_peduncle" title="Middle cerebellar peduncle">MCP</a> → <a href="/wiki/Deep_cerebellar_nuclei" title="Deep cerebellar nuclei">Deep cerebellar nuclei</a> → <a href="/wiki/Cerebellum_granule_cell" class="mw-redirect" title="Cerebellum granule cell">Granule cell</a></li></ul>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Inferior_olivary_nucleus" title="Inferior olivary nucleus">Inferior olivary nucleus</a> →  <b><a href="/wiki/Olivocerebellar_tract" title="Olivocerebellar tract">Olivocerebellar tract</a></b> → <a href="/wiki/Inferior_cerebellar_peduncle" title="Inferior cerebellar peduncle">ICP</a> → <a href="/wiki/Cerebellar_hemisphere" title="Cerebellar hemisphere">Hemisphere</a> → <a href="/wiki/Purkinje_cell" title="Purkinje cell">Purkinje cell</a> → <a href="/wiki/Deep_cerebellar_nuclei" title="Deep cerebellar nuclei">Deep cerebellar nuclei</a></li></ul>
</div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="navbox-group" style="width:1%">Efferent</th><td class="navbox-list-with-group navbox-list navbox-even" style="width:100%;padding:0"><div style="padding:0 0.25em">
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Dentate_nucleus" title="Dentate nucleus">Dentate nucleus</a> in <a href="/wiki/Cerebellar_hemisphere" title="Cerebellar hemisphere">Lateral hemisphere/pontocerebellum</a> → <a href="/wiki/Superior_cerebellar_peduncle" title="Superior cerebellar peduncle">SCP</a> → <b><a href="/wiki/Dentatothalamic_tract" title="Dentatothalamic tract">Dentatothalamic tract</a></b> → <a class="mw-selflink selflink">Thalamus</a> (<a href="/wiki/Ventral_lateral_nucleus" title="Ventral lateral nucleus">VL</a>) → <a href="/wiki/Motor_cortex" title="Motor cortex">Motor cortex</a></li></ul>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Interposed_nucleus" title="Interposed nucleus">Interposed nucleus</a> in <a href="/wiki/Cerebellar_hemisphere" title="Cerebellar hemisphere">Intermediate hemisphere/spinocerebellum</a> → <a href="/wiki/Superior_cerebellar_peduncle" title="Superior cerebellar peduncle">SCP</a> → <a href="/wiki/Reticular_formation" title="Reticular formation">Reticular formation</a>, or → <b><a href="/wiki/Cerebellothalamic_tract" title="Cerebellothalamic tract">Cerebellothalamic tract</a></b> → <a href="/wiki/Red_nucleus" title="Red nucleus">Red nucleus</a> → <a class="mw-selflink selflink">Thalamus</a> (<a href="/wiki/Ventral_lateral_nucleus" title="Ventral lateral nucleus">VL</a>) → <a href="/wiki/Motor_cortex" title="Motor cortex">Motor cortex</a></li></ul>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Fastigial_nucleus" title="Fastigial nucleus">Fastigial nucleus</a> in <a href="/wiki/Flocculonodular_lobe" title="Flocculonodular lobe">Flocculonodular lobe/vestibulocerebellum</a> → <b><a href="/wiki/Vestibulocerebellar_tract" title="Vestibulocerebellar tract">Vestibulocerebellar tract</a></b> → <a href="/wiki/Vestibular_nuclei" title="Vestibular nuclei">Vestibular nuclei</a></li></ul>
</div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="navbox-group" style="width:1%">Bidirectional:<br /><a href="/wiki/Spinocerebellar_tract" class="mw-redirect" title="Spinocerebellar tract">Spinocerebellar</a></th><td class="navbox-list-with-group navbox-list navbox-odd" style="width:100%;padding:0"><div style="padding:0 0.25em"></div><table class="nowraplinks navbox-subgroup" style="border-spacing:0"><tbody><tr><th scope="row" class="navbox-group" style="width:1%"><a href="/wiki/Proprioception#Conscious_and_unconscious_proprioception" title="Proprioception">Unconscious<br /> proprioception</a></th><td class="navbox-list-with-group navbox-list navbox-odd" style="width:100%;padding:0"><div style="padding:0 0.25em">
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Lower_limb" class="mw-redirect" title="Lower limb">lower limb</a> → 1° (<a href="/wiki/Muscle_spindle" title="Muscle spindle">muscle spindles</a> → <a href="/wiki/Dorsal_root_ganglion" title="Dorsal root ganglion">DRG</a>) → 2° (<a href="/wiki/Posterior_thoracic_nucleus" title="Posterior thoracic nucleus">Posterior thoracic nucleus</a> → <b><a href="/wiki/Dorsal_spinocerebellar_tract" class="mw-redirect" title="Dorsal spinocerebellar tract">Dorsal/posterior spinocerebellar tract</a></b> → <a href="/wiki/Inferior_cerebellar_peduncle" title="Inferior cerebellar peduncle">ICP</a> → <a href="/wiki/Cerebellar_vermis" title="Cerebellar vermis">Cerebellar vermis</a>)</li></ul>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Upper_limb" title="Upper limb">upper limb</a> → 1° (<a href="/wiki/Muscle_spindle" title="Muscle spindle">muscle spindles</a> → <a href="/wiki/Dorsal_root_ganglion" title="Dorsal root ganglion">DRG</a>) → 2° (<a href="/wiki/Accessory_cuneate_nucleus" title="Accessory cuneate nucleus">Accessory cuneate nucleus</a> → <b><a href="/wiki/Posterior_external_arcuate_fibers" class="mw-redirect" title="Posterior external arcuate fibers">Cuneocerebellar tract</a></b> → <a href="/wiki/Inferior_cerebellar_peduncle" title="Inferior cerebellar peduncle">ICP</a> → <a href="/wiki/Anterior_lobe_of_cerebellum" title="Anterior lobe of cerebellum">Anterior lobe of cerebellum</a>)</li></ul>
</div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="navbox-group" style="width:1%"><a href="/wiki/Reflex_arc" title="Reflex arc">Reflex arc</a></th><td class="navbox-list-with-group navbox-list navbox-even" style="width:100%;padding:0"><div style="padding:0 0.25em">
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Lower_limb" class="mw-redirect" title="Lower limb">lower limb</a> → 1° (<a href="/wiki/Golgi_tendon_organ" title="Golgi tendon organ">Golgi tendon organ</a>) → 2° (<b><a href="/wiki/Ventral_spinocerebellar_tract" class="mw-redirect" title="Ventral spinocerebellar tract">Ventral/anterior spinocerebellar tract</a></b>→ <a href="/wiki/Superior_cerebellar_peduncle" title="Superior cerebellar peduncle">SCP</a> → <a href="/wiki/Cerebellar_vermis" title="Cerebellar vermis">Cerebellar vermis</a>)</li></ul>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Upper_limb" title="Upper limb">upper limb</a> → 1° (<a href="/wiki/Golgi_tendon_organ" title="Golgi tendon organ">Golgi tendon organ</a>) → 2° (<b><a href="/wiki/Rostral_spinocerebellar_tract" class="mw-redirect" title="Rostral spinocerebellar tract">Rostral spinocerebellar tract</a></b> → <a href="/wiki/Inferior_cerebellar_peduncle" title="Inferior cerebellar peduncle">ICP</a> → <a href="/wiki/Cerebellum" title="Cerebellum">Cerebellum</a>)</li></ul>
